<div id="review_526721424" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526721424" />
    <a title="Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3399699-rose"><img alt="Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386022874p2/3399699.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/526721424?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rose" href="/user/show/3399699-rose">Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3399699-rose?shelf=dropped-series">dropped-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer526721424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9853811045824567657"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I think I'll need a night to meditate on my thoughts on this, but it's likely to be 1 star. It's pretty much a tough issues story that isn't very realistic and has probably two of the most formulaic protagonists I've read in the genre. I wish I could say I felt more for it, but the narrative had a lot of problems.<br/><br/><b>Full review:</b><br/><br/>In the aftermath, I can say that I gave my first read from Jessica Sorensen a try with an open mind. It won't be the last I read from her bibliography beca</span>
  <span id="freeText9853811045824567657" style="display:none"><b>Initial reaction:</b> I think I'll need a night to meditate on my thoughts on this, but it's likely to be 1 star. It's pretty much a tough issues story that isn't very realistic and has probably two of the most formulaic protagonists I've read in the genre. I wish I could say I felt more for it, but the narrative had a lot of problems.<br /><br /><b>Full review:</b><br /><br />In the aftermath, I can say that I gave my first read from Jessica Sorensen a try with an open mind. It won't be the last I read from her bibliography because I own two of her other novels and I don't really have a handle on her style yet. But I'll admit this was rough. I couldn't find much value in it beyond the usual formula. New Adult novel where the hero and heroine have problems/tragic pasts, no one says anything about said problems and that further complicates the situation. Hero and heroine meet up in college, add in gay sidekick for spice, hero and heroine have <s>frequent</s> awkward sex, and then ending cliffhanger: hero does something really stupid and heroine is grief-stricken.<br /><br />Wait...what?<br /><br />I'll take this space to explain because there is a bit more to it than that, but it doesn't handle its themes all that well despite taking on some vital issues. (And the editing in this wasn't very good to boot, but that's another issue on top of the major story ones.) <br /><br />Callie and Kayden both have tragic pasts in the form of abuse at the hands of people in their inner circles. For Callie, it's sexual abuse, for Kayden, it's physical. The two suffer in silence and have had their worlds shattered as a result. They know each other loosely because Callie stopped one horrible event from happening by showing up at a party looking to pull her brother out. Fast forward some time later, they meet again in college.<br /><br />Callie's a difficult character to like despite her circumstances. She frequently slut shames and her personality is about as interesting as watching paint dry. Kayden's situation is harsh, but I'll admit even as I'm reflecting over the experience of reading this, I have a hard time remembering much about him other than his easy dialogues with Callie and the fact that he engages in awkward sex with Callie in his attempt to "heal" her.<br /><br />I felt numb reading this in spells because it was one dramatic factor after another, leading up to the last part of the book which was a cruel cliffhanger for events. The ending wasn't even really an ending, more like the point which the book stopped and then you have to read the next part to know what happened.<br /><br />Suffice to say, I can't really continue with this series because the characters felt so formulaic, the emotional resonance so contrived that it didn't do anything for me.<br /><br />Overall score: 0.5/5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="9853811045824567657" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_462683783" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462683783" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462683783?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5481477-rachel?shelf=netgalley-e-book">netgalley-e-book</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462683783" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13618007884509084931"><b>The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden</b> may sound like your typical New Adult but somehow this was done so much better than most. The story swept me up and didn’t let me go! It filled my heart with emotions and intensity!<br/><br/>Callie and Kayden have known each other for years, going to the same school. Their families have even socialized on and off. But they’ve never traveled in the same social circles with Kayden being the popular high school football quarterback and Callie being the school recluse/frea</span>
  <span id="freeText13618007884509084931" style="display:none"><b>The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden</b> may sound like your typical New Adult but somehow this was done so much better than most. The story swept me up and didn’t let me go! It filled my heart with emotions and intensity!<br /><br />Callie and Kayden have known each other for years, going to the same school. Their families have even socialized on and off. But they’ve never traveled in the same social circles with Kayden being the popular high school football quarterback and Callie being the school recluse/freak since she was twelve. However, Callie makes an impression on Kayden when she saves his life. He doesn’t get a chance to thank her because just a few days after, she goes off to college early to attend summer session. Being gone from her home can’t happen a minute too soon for Callie. Ever since her twelfth birthday it hasn’t been the normal sanctuary that most homes provide for children. <br /><br />Callie doesn’t think she’ll lay eyes on Kayden again after saving him, and she certainly doesn’t expect Kayden would ever think a thing about her. Callie couldn’t be more wrong. Little does she know Kayden has suffered growing up as well, except all his suffering has been hidden, and that one night when she bothered to care is something he’ll never forget. <br /><br />Like I said, the idea of this story is really nothing new in New Adult category, but it stands out from the rest in execution. The effects from the traumas that both Callie and Kayden went through felt very authentic. Ms. Sorensen wrote characters that felt very real and so it was easy to connect to, put myself in their shoes, and root for their happiness! Their emotions, pain, and new tentative hope come through clearly thanks to the dual POVs. <br /><br />When they strike up a friendship in college, knowledge of Kayden’s past pain allows Callie to share her own, and their shared burden makes it easier to bear, cope, and heal. The romance was timidly and cautiously allowed, and I felt completely appropriate for the situation. With that being said there were still passionate, intense, and lusty moments to relish:<br /><b>
  <i><br />“No, I don’t like you better this way. I like the sober Callie, the one that I can talk to. The one that is so sweet it’s f**king adorable.” I dip my face forward and breathe on her neck, moving toward the no touching line, but not crossing it. “The one that trembles just from the feel of my breath. The one that I want to kiss and touch so f**king badly it drives me crazy. The one that makes me feel things…”<br /></i>
</b><br />Anxiousness kept me at the edge of my seat at times. Callie and Kayden’s traumas are hidden and secret, and others want them to stay that way. I was nervous and worried over what might happen when and if they came out. <br /><br />Fair warning, this does end in a cliffhanger. I had the second one ready to go so I wasn’t worried. I also found out that the blurb for The Redemption of Callie and Kayden (book 2) alleviates some concerns, but I wouldn’t read it if you haven’t read the first. Best of all, the second book releases August 6th, so there’s very little wait time if you decide to read this now. If you have any inclination toward New Adult reads, this is one I would pick up for sure. I loved it! <br /><br /><i>A copy was provided by Forever through Netgalley in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />You can read this review and more on <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/07/review-coincidence-of-callie-kayden-by.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den.</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13618007884509084931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_513221840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/513221840" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2871271-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1258152693p2/2871271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/513221840?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/2871271-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=cringe-inducing">cringe-inducing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=issues">issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=triggering-topics">triggering-topics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=abandoned-dnf">abandoned-dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=read-in-2013">read-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=0-stars">0-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2871271-angela?shelf=trauma-porn-romance">trauma-porn-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer513221840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10572261311461438458"><br/><b>
  <i>Poor writing & implausible story made this a non-finisher for me</i>
</b><br/><br/>In an attempt to try out another New Adult title, I downloaded <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16113791.The_Coincidence_of_Callie_and_Kayden__The_Coincidence___1_' title='The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden (The Coincidence, #1) by Jessica Sorensen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden</a>. It is currently sitting in the #4 spot on the NYT Best Sellers list for e-books, and it seemed like a deal at only 99 cents. I even picked up the author's second similar title (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15717876.The_Secret_of_Ella_and_Micha__The_Secret___1_' title='The Secret of Ella and Micha (The Secret, #1) by Jessica Sorensen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Secret of Ella and Micha</a>) on a whim at the same time. Though I should have been more wary due to the low price and the author's self-pubbed status, I </span>
  <span id="freeText10572261311461438458" style="display:none"><br /><b>
  <i>Poor writing &amp; implausible story made this a non-finisher for me</i>
</b><br /><br />In an attempt to try out another New Adult title, I downloaded <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16113791.The_Coincidence_of_Callie_and_Kayden__The_Coincidence___1_" title="The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden (The Coincidence, #1) by Jessica Sorensen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden</a>. It is currently sitting in the #4 spot on the NYT Best Sellers list for e-books, and it seemed like a deal at only 99 cents. I even picked up the author's second similar title (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15717876.The_Secret_of_Ella_and_Micha__The_Secret___1_" title="The Secret of Ella and Micha (The Secret, #1) by Jessica Sorensen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Secret of Ella and Micha</a>) on a whim at the same time. Though I should have been more wary due to the low price and the author's self-pubbed status, I was feeling adventurous.<br /><br />Oh, how wary I should have been! I have never before given up on a title so quickly as I did with this book (at the 7% completion mark). The two chapters that I read were littered with typos, incorrect pronoun usage, and simply pedestrian and awkward writing. As per usual with YA or NA titles, the characters have trials or past abuses to overcome, but this story laid them out entirely too obviously within the first three pages with clunky statements about "hiding the scars on the inside" and the young woman's obvious fear of men. Then, soon after we're told that the main character hasn't touched anyone outside her family in six years and has never told a soul about what trauma has befallen her, the next chapter finds her at college with a new best friend -- the token gay guy -- whom she touches, laughs with, and has shared her darkest secrets with. The quick character changes, and the obviously forthcoming romance with the also-traumatized football jock from her hometown, just seemed too unbelievable. I simply had to stop reading due to the absolute implausibility of the story and the poor writing. <br /><br />Though I don't hope to diminish anyone else's interest or enthusiasm for this book, I can't understand any of the hype, high sales, or great ratings for this book and the author's other titles, if they are at all similar. Not only did I declare this a DNF title, but it is also the first thing I have ever digitally returned. Read at your own risk.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10572261311461438458" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1443872343313739906">This was a YA/NA contemporary romance which also dealt with the hard-hitting topics of rape and child abuse.<br/><br/>I thought Callie did a pretty good job of handling what had happened in her past, and trying to get on with her future, even if it involved a little bit of running away. I felt sorry for her for what she had been through though, and the bullying she received at school seemed unfair also after she had been through so much.<br/><br/>The storyline in this followed Callie as she went to college, and Kay</span>
  <span id="freeText1443872343313739906" style="display:none">This was a YA/NA contemporary romance which also dealt with the hard-hitting topics of rape and child abuse.<br /><br />I thought Callie did a pretty good job of handling what had happened in her past, and trying to get on with her future, even if it involved a little bit of running away. I felt sorry for her for what she had been through though, and the bullying she received at school seemed unfair also after she had been through so much.<br /><br />The storyline in this followed Callie as she went to college, and Kayden as he eventually joined her. We had storyline which dealt with the topics of rape, child abuse, and self-harm, and this pair really did not have an easy life.<br /><br />There was romance between Callie and Kayden, and a couple of sexy scenes which were worth reading.<br /><br />The ending to this was a big cliff-hanger, so I’m going to have to read the next book to find out what happens.<br />6 out of 10</span>

<div id="review_461004385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/461004385" />
    <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie"><img alt="Natasha is a Book Junkie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585046882p2/9389992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/461004385?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natasha is a Book Junkie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natasha is a Book Junkie" href="/user/show/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie">Natasha is a Book Junkie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9389992-natasha-is-a-book-junkie?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer461004385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14025122409958423061"><blockquote>
  <p>
    <b>
      <i>“… the thing I regret - will always regret - is going into my room on my twelfth birthday.”</i>
    </b>
  </p>
</blockquote><br/>Nothing will prepare you for what this book is about or the authenticity with which it tackles some very important but grim life issues. This is a book about second chances at what life should have been in the first place, about the freeing power of the human connection, and about love between wounded souls.<br/><br/>Callie and Kayden lived in the same small town all their lives, went to the </span>
  <span id="freeText14025122409958423061" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <p>
    <b>
      <i>“… the thing I regret - will always regret - is going into my room on my twelfth birthday.”</i>
    </b>
  </p>
</blockquote><br />Nothing will prepare you for what this book is about or the authenticity with which it tackles some very important but grim life issues. This is a book about second chances at what life should have been in the first place, about the freeing power of the human connection, and about love between wounded souls.<br /><br />Callie and Kayden lived in the same small town all their lives, went to the same school, knew the same people, but they have never really known each other. Their paths rarely crossed, their lives rarely intersected, but they knew of each other. One tragic encounter between them just before moving out of home and going to college connects their lives irrevocably, planting the seed for everything that happens between them afterwards.<br /><br />Callie and Kayden’s lives have been everything but ordinary. Each one of them carries the burden of their own secrets, recognising in each other the sadness that comes from carrying such burden from a young age. They've both felt so much ugliness and endured such emotional pain in their young lives that they've become afraid of feeling intense emotions again. They choose numbness and avoidance over confronting the source of their pain. They swipe it all under the rug and face life fiercely guarding their internal turmoil. Their shame over what happened to them further taints their happiness, always making them feel incomplete and ruined.<br /><br />Kayden is a product of constant and systematic physical abuse by the hand of a man who should have been his protector, not his worst nightmare. Abuse and fear were the only language spoken in his home while growing up, but while his brothers eventually either retaliated or left without ever looking back, Kayden endured his sentence alone, never reacting, pain becoming a source of emotional escape rather than a reason to run. It became his dirty little secret, a coping mechanism for whenever he could not deal with too many emotions together.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“As his fist hammers against my face, warm blood pours along my skin and splatters against his shirt. I know this time he’s probably going to kill me and I should finally fight back, but I was taught to die on the inside. Plus I just don’t seem to care anymore.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Callie's abuse, on the other hand, might have been a one-off occurrence in her life, but its effects on her wounded mind have followed her ever since, shaping her interaction with others, her appearance, self-esteem, but most of all, her trust in people, including those closest to her. No one had saved her during that horrific act when her innocence was stolen from her and she has never trusted another person since. She spent the remainder of her forming years hiding from the world, attempting to disappear and blend into the shadows. Callie has her own ways of dealing with her pain, just as desperate and just as self-destructive as Kayden’s. They have so much in common without even realising it.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Everyone was watching me, like they could see that I wasn’t whole anymore.”</i>
</blockquote><br />When they meet again in college, they are both terrified of the pull between them. By spending time together, Callie soon realizes that Kayden makes her feel safe, protected. Their growing intimacy slowly purges her mind from her bad memories, replacing them with new, happy ones. Kayden, however, fights his attraction to her, recognizing the way she makes him feel as something that could potentially shake his careless façade.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“… from the few moments I’ve spent with her, I’ve felt everything too much… she makes me feel things I’m not used to; the dirty dreams, the protectiveness, the way my stupid heart starts to beat like it’s finally alive.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Two broken hearts start to heal by simply caring for each other and acknowledging each other’s demons. Their connection is primal, irreversible, addictive. They offer each other a way out of the darkness they’ve been living in, fiercely protecting one another from further abuse and soothing existing wounds with compassion and kindness. But life can be excessively cruel to the ones that deserve it the least and soon Kayden and Callie are again battling old fiends.<br /><br />A compelling and superbly written story that will keep you captivated and consumed by truly loveable characters and a storyline that will undoubtedly leave its mark on your heart. The sequel is planned for release in early 2013.<br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Life is full of luck, like getting dealt a good hand, or simply by being in the right place at the right time. Some people get luck handed to them, a second chance, a save. It can happen heroically, or by a simple coincidence, but there are those who don’t get luck on a shiny platter, who end up in the wrong place at the wrong time, who don’t get saved.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />~ N ♥<br /><br /><a href="http://wp.me/p2AtqW-Ip" rel="nofollow noopener">See this review on my blog!</a> | <a href="http://www.facebook.com/natashaisabookjunkie" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Facebook!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14025122409958423061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_478185099" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478185099" />
    <a title="Ava" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5832186-ava"><img alt="Ava" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478185099?book_show_action=true">Dec 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ava" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ava" href="/user/show/5832186-ava">Ava</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=two-stars">two-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=realistic-fiction-romance">realistic-fiction-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5832186-ava?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478185099" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15626056190806641745">It seems that I've been comparing every book with 'broken main characters' lately to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.PUSHING_THE_LIMITS__Pushing_the_Limits___1_' title='PUSHING THE LIMITS (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>PUSHING THE LIMITS</a>, which was a perfect example for novels of that topic, even though I didn't love it.<br/><br/>The plot is terribly cliché. I think we've all read that story about the traumatized heroine and the abused hero, or vice-versa. The whole books consists of Callie forcing Kayden away, then beckoning him back, and pushing him away again, and Kayden leaving, then more making out - but pretty much chock-full of e</span>
  <span id="freeText15626056190806641745" style="display:none">It seems that I've been comparing every book with 'broken main characters' lately to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.PUSHING_THE_LIMITS__Pushing_the_Limits___1_" title="PUSHING THE LIMITS (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">PUSHING THE LIMITS</a>, which was a perfect example for novels of that topic, even though I didn't love it.<br /><br />The plot is terribly cliché. I think we've all read that story about the traumatized heroine and the abused hero, or vice-versa. The whole books consists of Callie forcing Kayden away, then beckoning him back, and pushing him away again, and Kayden leaving, then more making out - but pretty much chock-full of eye-rolling angst.<br /><br />It had a serious cliffhanger ending. I actually kept on skipping after the last page to check if there was an epilogue, because holy hell. That was some serious shit that shows you right there that love can't save you all the time. <br /><br />I can't really say anything about Callie except that she annoyed the hell out of me, and her constant, pointless slut-shaming (or just girlfriend-shaming, to be honest) did not help me sympathize with her character. Yes, horrible things happened to her, but she didn't need to be so unlikable, either.<br /><br />Kayden was just a 'meh' for me. He wanted to protect Callie all the time, and I guess he has to because she certainly isn't a strong main character. I didn't find him interesting or swoon-worthy at all, though I did feel terrible for him.<br /><br />I really liked Seth, even if he was a stereotypical gay guy. <s>But a lot of my gay friends are like that, so whatever.</s> Bubbly, fun, and cute, he was probably the only character that didn't make me want to punch a wall.<br /><br />The other characters were mostly dull and forgettable. <br /><br />The writing was simple to read and kind of amateur. There were contextual and grammatical errors, and while Callie's journal entries were supposed to be thought-provoking , mature, and beautiful, I found them rather cheesy.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"In the existence of our lives, there is a single coincidence that brings us together and for a moment, our hearts beat as one."</i>
</blockquote><br />Yeah... I don't know about you guys, but I really snorted when I read that. Sorry for disappointing you.<br /><br />A boring read for me. I don't have a lot to say about it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15626056190806641745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

First and foremost they behave as friends, The cuteness overload making their story story even more memorable.<b>They talk more than hashtags and emojis. <div id="review_1102328601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1102328601?book_show_action=true">Nov 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Pearl Angeli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Pearl Angeli" href="/user/show/31514572-pearl-angeli">Pearl Angeli</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780751552607" href="/book/show/18591022-the-coincidence-of-callie-and-kayden">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=owned-physical-copy">owned-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=hot-male-characters">hot-male-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=new-adult-contemporary">new-adult-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=cute-book-couple">cute-book-couple</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=fangirling">fangirling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31514572-pearl-angeli?shelf=highly-recommended-na">highly-recommended-na</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1102328601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15454489129326166522"> <i>
  <b>Callie saved me that night from a fight that would have probably left me dead, but she also saved me from myself. Before her, I was dying inside; there was nothing in my heart, but an empty hole.</b>
</i> <br/><br/>This is without a doubt, one of the best New Adult - Contemporary books I've had so far. I love everything in The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden! It's one of those books that have everything you want in a contemporary read that will leave you feeling awed. It's just *sigh* perfect!<br/><br/>If you want to </span>
  <span id="freeText15454489129326166522" style="display:none"> <i>
  <b>Callie saved me that night from a fight that would have probably left me dead, but she also saved me from myself. Before her, I was dying inside; there was nothing in my heart, but an empty hole.</b>
</i> <br /><br />This is without a doubt, one of the best New Adult - Contemporary books I've had so far. I love everything in The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden! It's one of those books that have everything you want in a contemporary read that will leave you feeling awed. It's just *sigh* perfect!<br /><br />If you want to read something that has to do with dark past and secrets with a bit of heavy drama and a sizzling romance, then this book is for you. I love how Jessica Sorensen evoked such deep emotions in me when I least expected it. The characters-- Kayden and Callie are one of the amazing characters I've met. The chemistry is seriously visible. And I love the fact that each time they interact, you can really feel the sexual tension between them.<br /><br />And let me tell you that the very first moment you'll meet the characters, you'll instantly feel the connection. They're two troubled, f*cked up characters with emotional wounds that will really tug your heart. And oh, the romance is good. Every freaking kissing and make-out details of Callie and Kayden is emotional and moving you will basically find yourself hanging on to every word the author writes.<br /><br />After reading the book, I had a very huge desire to find the second installment and grab another bite 'coz ugh, it feels not enough. The ending is a total cliffhanger (though I really don't mind). :)<br /><br />As a whole, The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden is totally a must-read.<br /><br /> <i>
  <b>"In the existence of our lives, there is a single coincidence that brings us together and for a moment, our hearts beat as one."</b>
</i> <br /><br />My Rating for this Book: 5 Stars<br /><br />Book review also posted on my blog:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/2014/11/30/review-the-coincidence-of-callie-and-kayden-by-jessica-sorensen/">https://bibliopearl.wordpress.com/201...</a></span>

<div id="review_497707709" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/497707709" />
    <a title="~Mindy Lynn~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7320000-mindy-lynn"><img alt="~Mindy Lynn~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604190846p2/7320000.jpg" /></a>

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403878ra/785829.gif" alt="new girl gifs photo: ng_pretzels.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>I ALMOST FLUNG MY PHONE ACROSS THE ROOM! I.. I.. I DON'T EVEN KNOW HOW TO COMPREHEND WHAT JUST HAPPENED!</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/new%20girl%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403878ra/785830.gif" alt="new girl gifs photo: New Girl - Jess - What is Your Problem tumblr_mil455FqHA1s6zr09o1_500_zpsa63266c6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>WHO DOES THAT TO THEIR READERS? HOW CAN YOU LEAVE ME HANGING LIKE THAT? MY FIRST THOUGHT WAS THAT I SKIPPED SOME PAGES, BUT NOPE! IT JUST ENDS LIKE I WAS DROPPED OFF AN EDGE OF A CLIFF.</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/new%20girl%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403878ra/785831.gif" alt="new girl gifs photo: New Girl - Jess - Ugly Crying tumblr_inline_mknkedlOfG1qz4rgp_zpseacbc94d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>I NEED THE NEXT BOOK NOW!</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/NEW%20GIRL%20GIFS" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403878ra/785832.gif" alt="NEW GIRL GIFS photo: New Girl - Nick - A Little Broken tumblr_mgqc3necWu1qeekseo1_500_zps219eca28.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>*SIGH*</b><br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/new%20girl%20gifs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380403878ra/785833.gif" alt="new girl gifs photo: ng_shock.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>The Coincidence of Callie and Kayden</i>
</b> ended up being one of those stories that left me completely undone. The emotions this book put me through had me at extreme highs and lows. But I loved every minute of it.<br>Kayden is living in a home where abuse is as normal as breathing. Callie is living in a home where it is better to don’t ask and don’t tell. Both of their mother’s live in complete denial. This leaves them both closed off to deal with their melancholy in silence. <br> The story of Callie and Kayden is raw and intense. The story isn’t an easy one to read. The event’s that have and that are still happening to these characters have them both coping in very unhealthy ways. But as dark as the story is, it also had some humor, which made this story, all around, one of my favorites that I have read this year. When a book cuts you open and has you spilling as many emotions as this book did to me it is hard to not absolutely love it. <br>But something I didn’t love was the ending. Not that it ended horribly, well yes it did. The reason it did is because it left me with the biggest cliff-hanger I have ever been left hanging onto while ending a book. The emotions after swiping the last page were complete disbelief. I couldn’t read through those last pages fast enough. My heart was beating fast with anxiety for these characters and then it just ends with no relief. It gutted me and left me open feeling everything from aw to anger that the author could just leave me that last page and offer me no kind of closure. But now, sitting here writing this, the anger has subsided more and I am back to the ‘aw’ moment. Because the story is one I for sure will never forget and one I will forever be glad that I purchased. There are only so many books that leave a thumbprint on your life and this book will be one of those for me. I am very eager to read the next book and I have already pre-ordered it. I need to know what happens! <br><br></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer462081168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18304675713485777011"><b>“In the existence of our lives, there is a single coincidence that brings us together and for a moment, our hearts beat as one.”</b><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398568i/770441._SY540_.jpg' width='300' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>“Seize the day, take hold of it, and make it whatever you want.”</b><br/><br/><br/>Seriously, I really liked this story. I love to torture myself with a good YA/NA broken boy/girl book and this one did not disappoint. Loved that Callie found a friend (Seth) to help her on the road to healing; the list was an awesome tool for them. <br/>This list opened up many opportunities for Callie to begin</span>
  <span id="freeText18304675713485777011" style="display:none"><b>“In the existence of our lives, there is a single coincidence that brings us together and for a moment, our hearts beat as one.”</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380398568i/770441._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>“Seize the day, take hold of it, and make it whatever you want.”</b><br><br><br>Seriously, I really liked this story. I love to torture myself with a good YA/NA broken boy/girl book and this one did not disappoint. Loved that Callie found a friend (Seth) to help her on the road to healing; the list was an awesome tool for them. <br>This list opened up many opportunities for Callie to begin to let Kayden in and it was really sweet and sad how they came together and began to love. <br><br>#17 Let Something Amazing Happen, Without Question or Hesitation<br><br>#3 Be Stupidly, Drunk Happy<br><br>#9 Dance in the Rain #13 Live in the Moment #17 Be Yourself<br>(Yeah, I noticed a few repeat list #’s. So what, still loved them) <br><br>There were many angsty and disturbing scenes that make this book one of those books I put in my “made-me-feel” shelf and of course we (I) will also be putting this book in my "cliffy" shelf because it really left me hanging… <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398568ra/770442.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But... I know I have the next book to look forward to as well as many more by this author, Jessica Sorensen... Love Her!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EDiXrWRgbypBtpoi/QkgK4NG/M7nNkQVhsybiFYGRn/y8UvJkKcXIv5c0hKdeMGryjphSgdYGL6CWasc4V+Tkg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('M/ro7NvIItNvuGHDoj/JpC2oD+VlG0FGd6IH/ksNNqvRMzSILw9a29BSKfPCTigkZNSSYYV1He1zNzdq/FTjRg==')})
  }
